	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" >Larry Ellison</h1>
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"><div id="mw-fr-revisiontag" class="flaggedrevs_short flaggedrevs_stable_synced plainlinks noprint"><div class="flaggedrevs_short_basic"><span aria-disabled='false' title='Changes must be reviewed before being displayed on this page.' class='flaggedrevs-icon oo-ui-widget oo-ui-widget-enabled oo-ui-iconElement-icon oo-ui-icon-articleSearch oo-ui-iconElement oo-ui-labelElement-invisible oo-ui-iconWidget'></span><span id='mw-fr-revisiontoggle' aria-disabled='false' title='show/hide details' class='fr-toggle-arrow oo-ui-widget oo-ui-widget-enabled oo-ui-indicatorElement-indicator oo-ui-indicator-down oo-ui-indicatorElement oo-ui-labelElement-invisible oo-ui-indicatorWidget'></span></div>

<p><b>Lawrence Joseph Ellison</b> (born August 17, 1944) is an American business magnate, investor, and philanthropist who is a co-founder, the executive chairman and chief technology officer (CTO) of <a href="/wiki/Oracle_Corporation" title="Oracle Corporation">Oracle Corporation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> As of October 2019, he was listed by <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> magazine as the fourth-wealthiest person in the United States and as the sixth-wealthiest in the world, with a fortune of $69.1&#160;billion, increased from $54.5&#160;billion in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-Larry_Ellison_topic_page_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Larry_Ellison_topic_page-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> He is also the owner of the 41st largest island in the United States, <a href="/wiki/Lanai" title="Lanai">Lanai</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Hawaiian_Islands" title="Hawaiian Islands">Hawaiian Islands</a> with a population of just over 3000.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life_and_education">Early life and education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Larry_Ellison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life and education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Larry Ellison was born in New York City, to an unwed <a href="/wiki/Jewish" class="mw-redirect" title="Jewish">Jewish</a> mother.<sup id="cite_ref-Jspace_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jspace-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ell_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ell-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> His biological father was an Italian-American <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army_Air_Corps" title="United States Army Air Corps">United States Army Air Corps</a> pilot. After Ellison contracted <a href="/wiki/Pneumonia" title="Pneumonia">pneumonia</a> at the age of nine months, his mother gave him to her aunt and uncle for adoption.<sup id="cite_ref-ell_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ell-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> He did not meet his biological mother again until he was 48.<sup id="cite_ref-Rohrlich_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rohrlich-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Ellison moved to Chicago's <a href="/wiki/South_Shore,_Chicago" title="South Shore, Chicago">South Shore</a>, then a middle-class neighborhood. He remembers his adoptive mother as warm and loving, in contrast to his austere, unsupportive, and often distant adoptive father, who had chosen  the name Ellison to honor his point of entry into the United States, <a href="/wiki/Ellis_Island" title="Ellis Island">Ellis Island</a>. Louis Ellison was a government employee who had made a small fortune in Chicago real estate, only to lose it during the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ell_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ell-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Although Ellison was raised in a <a href="/wiki/Reform_Judaism" title="Reform Judaism">Reform Jewish</a> home by his adoptive parents, who attended synagogue regularly, he remained a religious skeptic. Ellison states: "While I think I am religious in one sense, the particular dogmas of Judaism are not dogmas I subscribe to. I don't believe that they are real. They're interesting stories. They're interesting mythology, and I certainly respect people who believe these are literally true, but I don't. I see no evidence for this stuff." At age thirteen, Ellison refused to have a <a href="/wiki/Bar_mitzvah" class="mw-redirect" title="Bar mitzvah">bar mitzvah</a> celebration.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Ellison says that his fondness for Israel is not connected to religious sentiments, but rather due to the innovative spirit of Israelis in the technology sector.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Ellison attended <a href="/wiki/South_Shore_High_School_(Chicago)" title="South Shore High School (Chicago)">South Shore High School</a> in Chicago<sup id="cite_ref-LRO_Softwar_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LRO_Softwar-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> and later was admitted to <a href="/wiki/University_of_Illinois_at_Urbana%E2%80%93Champaign" title="University of Illinois at Urbana–Champaign">University of Illinois at Urbana–Champaign</a> and was enrolled as a premed student.<sup id="cite_ref-LRO_Softwar_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LRO_Softwar-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> At Illinois, he was named science student of the year<sup id="cite_ref-Saleem_Lives_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Saleem_Lives-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Icons_Business_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Icons_Business-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> but later withdrew without taking final exams after his sophomore year, because his adoptive mother had just died. After spending the summer of 1966 in California, he then attended the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Chicago" title="University of Chicago">University of Chicago</a> for one term, studying <a href="/wiki/Physics" title="Physics">physics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mathematics" title="Mathematics">mathematics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-LRO_Softwar_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LRO_Softwar-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> He did not take any exams and at Chicago he first encountered computer design. In 1966, aged 22, he moved to <a href="/wiki/Berkeley,_California" title="Berkeley, California">Berkeley, California</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_career_and_Oracle">Early career and Oracle</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Larry_Ellison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early career and Oracle">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Larry_Ellison_in_Oracle_OpenWorld_2010.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Larry_Ellison_in_Oracle_OpenWorld_2010.JPG/220px-Larry_Ellison_in_Oracle_OpenWorld_2010.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Larry_Ellison_in_Oracle_OpenWorld_2010.JPG/330px-Larry_Ellison_in_Oracle_OpenWorld_2010.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Larry_Ellison_in_Oracle_OpenWorld_2010.JPG/440px-Larry_Ellison_in_Oracle_OpenWorld_2010.JPG 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Larry_Ellison_in_Oracle_OpenWorld_2010.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Larry Ellison lecturing at the <a href="/wiki/Oracle_OpenWorld" title="Oracle OpenWorld">Oracle OpenWorld</a>, San Francisco 2010</div></div></div>
<p>While working at <a href="/wiki/Ampex" title="Ampex">Ampex</a> in the early 1970s, he became influenced by <a href="/wiki/Edgar_F._Codd" title="Edgar F. Codd">Edgar F. Codd</a>'s research on <a href="/wiki/Relational_database" title="Relational database">relational database</a> design, which led in 1977 to the formation of what became Oracle. Oracle became a successful database vendor to mid- and low-range systems, later competing with <a href="/wiki/Sybase" title="Sybase">Sybase</a> (created 1984) and <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_SQL_Server" title="Microsoft SQL Server">Microsoft SQL Server</a> (a port of Sybase created in 1989) which led to Ellison being listed by <i>Forbes</i> as one of the richest people in the world.
</p>
<h3><span id="1977.E2.80.931994"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1977–1994">1977–1994</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Larry_Ellison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 1977–1994">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>During the 1970s, after a brief stint at <a href="/wiki/Amdahl_Corporation" title="Amdahl Corporation">Amdahl Corporation</a>, Ellison began working for <a href="/wiki/Ampex_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Ampex Corporation">Ampex Corporation</a>. His projects included a <a href="/wiki/Database" title="Database">database</a> for the <a href="/wiki/CIA" class="mw-redirect" title="CIA">CIA</a>, which he named "Oracle". Ellison was inspired by a paper written by <a href="/wiki/Edgar_F._Codd" title="Edgar F. Codd">Edgar F. Codd</a> on <a href="/wiki/Relational_database_management_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Relational database management system">relational database systems</a> called "A Relational Model of Data for Large Shared Data Banks".<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> In 1977, he founded Software Development Laboratories (SDL) with two partners and an investment of $2,000; $1,200 of the money was his.
</p><p>In 1979, the company renamed itself Relational Software Inc., and in 1983, officially became Oracle Systems Corporation after its flagship product, the <a href="/wiki/Oracle_Database" title="Oracle Database">Oracle Database</a>. Ellison had heard about the <a href="/wiki/IBM_System_R" title="IBM System R">IBM System R</a> database, also based on Codd's theories, and wanted Oracle to achieve compatibility with it, but IBM made this impossible by refusing to share System R's code. The initial release of Oracle in 1979 was called Oracle 2; there was no Oracle 1.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> In 1990, Oracle laid off 10% of its workforce (about 400 people) because it was losing money.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> This crisis, which almost resulted in the company's bankruptcy, came about because of Oracle's "up-front" marketing strategy, in which sales people urged potential customers to buy the largest possible amount of software all at once. The sales people then booked the value of future license sales in the current quarter, thereby increasing their bonuses. This became a problem when the future sales subsequently failed to materialize. Oracle eventually had to restate its earnings twice, and had to settle <a href="/wiki/Class-action" class="mw-redirect" title="Class-action">class-action</a> lawsuits arising from its having overstated its earnings. Ellison would later say that Oracle had made "an incredible business mistake".<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Although IBM dominated the mainframe relational database market with its <a href="/wiki/IBM_DB2" class="mw-redirect" title="IBM DB2">DB2</a> and <a href="/wiki/IBM_SQL/DS" title="IBM SQL/DS">SQL/DS</a> database products, it delayed entering the market for a relational database on <a href="/wiki/Unix" title="Unix">Unix</a> and <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Windows" title="Microsoft Windows">Windows</a> operating systems. This left the door open for <a href="/wiki/Sybase" title="Sybase">Sybase</a>, Oracle, <a href="/wiki/Informix_Corporation" title="Informix Corporation">Informix</a>, and eventually <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a> to dominate mid-range systems and microcomputers. Around this time, Oracle fell behind Sybase. From 1990 to 1993, Sybase was the fastest-growing database company and the database industry's darling vendor, but soon it fell victim to <a href="/wiki/Merger_mania" title="Merger mania">merger mania</a>. Sybase's 1996 merger with Powersoft resulted in a loss of focus on its core database technology. In 1993, Sybase sold the rights to its database software running under the Windows operating system to Microsoft Corporation, which now markets it under the name "SQL Server".
</p><p>In his early years at Oracle, Larry Ellison was named an Award Recipient in the High Technology Category for the <a href="/wiki/Ernst_and_Young" class="mw-redirect" title="Ernst and Young">EY</a> Entrepreneur of the Year Program.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="1994.E2.80.932010"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1994–2010">1994–2010</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Larry_Ellison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 1994–2010">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Larry_Ellison_on_stage.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Larry_Ellison_on_stage.jpg/220px-Larry_Ellison_on_stage.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="184" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Larry_Ellison_on_stage.jpg/330px-Larry_Ellison_on_stage.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Larry_Ellison_on_stage.jpg/440px-Larry_Ellison_on_stage.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3073" data-file-height="2568" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Larry_Ellison_on_stage.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ellison in 2009</div></div></div>
<p>In 1994, Informix overtook Sybase and became Oracle's most important rival. The intense war between Informix CEO Phil White and Ellison was front-page Silicon Valley news for three years. In April 1997, Informix announced a major revenue shortfall and earnings restatements. Phil White eventually landed in jail, and <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a> absorbed Informix in 2001. Also in 1997, Ellison was made a director of <a href="/wiki/Apple_Computer" class="mw-redirect" title="Apple Computer">Apple Computer</a> after <a href="/wiki/Steve_Jobs" title="Steve Jobs">Steve Jobs</a> returned to the company. Ellison resigned in 2002. With the defeat of Informix and of Sybase, Oracle enjoyed years of industry dominance until the rise of Microsoft SQL Server in the late 1990s and IBM's acquisition of Informix Software in 2001 to complement their <a href="/wiki/IBM_DB2" class="mw-redirect" title="IBM DB2">DB2</a> database. As of 2013<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Larry_Ellison&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> Oracle's main competition for new database licenses on UNIX, <a href="/wiki/Linux" title="Linux">Linux</a>, and Windows operating systems comes from IBM's DB2 and from Microsoft SQL Server. IBM's DB2 still dominates the <a href="/wiki/Mainframe_computer" title="Mainframe computer">mainframe</a> database market.
</p><p>In 2005, Oracle Corporation paid Ellison a $975,000 salary, a $6,500,000 bonus, and other compensation of $955,100.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> In 2007, Ellison earned a total compensation of $61,180,524, which included a base salary of $1,000,000, a cash bonus of $8,369,000, and options granted of $50,087,100.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> In 2008, he earned a total compensation of $84,598,700, which included a base salary of $1,000,000, a cash bonus of $10,779,000, no stock grants, and options granted of $71,372,700.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> In the year ending May 31, 2009, he made $56.8&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-cut_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cut-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> In 2006, <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> ranked him as the richest Californian.<sup id="cite_ref-Larry_Ellison_topic_page_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Larry_Ellison_topic_page-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> In April 2009, after a tug-of-war with <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hewlett-Packard" title="Hewlett-Packard">Hewlett-Packard</a>, Oracle announced its intent to buy <a href="/wiki/Sun_Microsystems" title="Sun Microsystems">Sun Microsystems</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> On July 2, 2009, for the fourth year in a row, Oracle's board awarded Ellison another 7 million stock options.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> On August 22, 2009, it was reported that Ellison would be paid only <a href="/wiki/One-dollar_salary" title="One-dollar salary">$1 for his base salary for the fiscal year</a> of 2010, down from the $1,000,000 he was paid in fiscal 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-cut_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cut-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-salary_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-salary-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2010.E2.80.93present"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2010–present">2010–present</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Larry_Ellison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 2010–present">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> approved Oracle's acquisition of <a href="/wiki/Sun_Microsystems" title="Sun Microsystems">Sun Microsystems</a> on January 21, 2010, and agreed that Oracle's acquisition of Sun "has the potential to revitalize important assets and create new and innovative products".<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> The Sun acquisition also gave Oracle control of the popular <a href="/wiki/MySQL" title="MySQL">MySQL</a> open source database, which Sun had acquired in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> On August 9, 2010, Ellison denounced <a href="/wiki/Hewlett-Packard" title="Hewlett-Packard">Hewlett-Packard</a>'s board for firing CEO <a href="/wiki/Mark_Hurd" title="Mark Hurd">Mark Hurd</a>, writing that "the HP board just made the worst personnel decision since the idiots on the <a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc." title="Apple Inc.">Apple</a> board fired <a href="/wiki/Steve_Jobs" title="Steve Jobs">Steve Jobs</a> many years ago." (Ellison and Hurd were close personal friends.)<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Then on September 6, Oracle hired Mark Hurd as co-president alongside <a href="/wiki/Safra_Catz" title="Safra Catz">Safra Catz</a>. Ellison remained in his current role at Oracle.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2010, the <i>Forbes</i> <a href="/wiki/List_of_billionaires" class="mw-redirect" title="List of billionaires">list of billionaires</a> ranked Ellison as the sixth-richest person in the world and as the third-richest American, with an estimated net worth of US$28&#160;billion.<sup id="cite_ref-Larry_Ellison_topic_page_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Larry_Ellison_topic_page-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> On July 27, 2010, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wall_Street_Journal" title="The Wall Street Journal">The Wall Street Journal</a></i> reported that Ellison was the best-paid executive in the last decade, collecting a total compensation of US$1.84&#160;billion.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> In September 2011, Ellison was listed on the <i>Forbes</i> list of billionaires as the fifth richest man in the world and was still the third richest American, with a net worth of about $36.5&#160;billion. In September 2012, Ellison was again listed on the <i>Forbes</i> list of billionaires as the third richest American citizen, behind <a href="/wiki/Bill_Gates" title="Bill Gates">Bill Gates</a> and <a href="/wiki/Warren_Buffett" title="Warren Buffett">Warren Buffett</a>, with a net worth of $44&#160;billion. In October 2012, he was listed just behind <a href="/wiki/David_Hamilton_Koch" class="mw-redirect" title="David Hamilton Koch">David Hamilton Koch</a> as the eighth richest person in the world, according to the Bloomberg Billionaires Index.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Ellison owns stakes in <a href="/wiki/Salesforce.com" class="mw-redirect" title="Salesforce.com">Salesforce.com</a>, <a href="/wiki/NetSuite" title="NetSuite">NetSuite</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quark_Pharmaceuticals" title="Quark Pharmaceuticals">Quark Biotechnology Inc.</a> and <a href="/wiki/Astex_Pharmaceuticals" class="mw-redirect" title="Astex Pharmaceuticals">Astex Pharmaceuticals</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Being_Larry_Ellison_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Being_Larry_Ellison-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> In June 2012, Ellison agreed to buy 98&#160;percent of the Hawaiian island of <a href="/wiki/Lana%27i" class="mw-redirect" title="Lana&#39;i">Lana'i</a> from <a href="/wiki/David_Murdock" class="mw-redirect" title="David Murdock">David Murdock</a>'s company, <a href="/wiki/Castle_%26_Cooke" title="Castle &amp; Cooke">Castle &amp; Cooke</a>. The price was reported to be between $500&#160;million and $600&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> In 2005, Ellison agreed to settle a four-year-old insider-trading lawsuit by offering to pay $100&#160;million to charity in Oracle's name.<sup id="cite_ref-InfoWorld_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-InfoWorld-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2013, according to the <i><a href="/wiki/Wall_Street_Journal" class="mw-redirect" title="Wall Street Journal">Wall Street Journal</a></i>, Ellison earned $94.6&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> On September 18, 2014, Ellison appointed <a href="/wiki/Mark_Hurd" title="Mark Hurd">Mark Hurd</a> to CEO of Oracle from his former position as President; <a href="/wiki/Safra_Catz" title="Safra Catz">Safra Catz</a> was also made CEO, moving from her former role as CFO. Ellison assumed the positions of chief technology officer and executive chairman.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In November 2016, <a href="/wiki/Oracle_Corporation" title="Oracle Corporation">Oracle</a> bought NetSuite for $9.3&#160;billion. Ellison owned 35% of NetSuite at the time of the purchase making him $3.5&#160;billion personally.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2017, <i>Forbes</i> estimated that Ellison was the 4th richest person in tech.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In June 2018, Ellison's net worth was about $54.5&#160;billion, according to <i>Forbes</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In December 2018, Ellison became a director on the board of <a href="/wiki/Tesla,_Inc." title="Tesla, Inc.">Tesla, Inc.</a>, after purchasing 3 million shares earlier that year.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:1_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As of December 31, 2019, Ellison owns 36.2% of the shares of Oracle Corporation,<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> and 1.7% of the shares of <a href="/wiki/Tesla_Inc." class="mw-redirect" title="Tesla Inc.">Tesla</a>.
</p><p>In April 2020, he launched a wellness company Hawaiian Island <a href="/wiki/Lanai" title="Lanai">Lanai</a> called Sensei.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As of June 2020, Ellison is said to be the seventh wealthiest person in the world, with a net worth of $66.8 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In December 2020, his net worth increased by $2.5 billion in a single week as Oracle's stock jumped by 4% between November 27 and December 4.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Larry_Ellison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Ellison has been married and divorced four times:<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>Adda Quinn from 1967 to 1974.</li>
<li>Nancy Wheeler Jenkins from 1977 to 1978. They married six months before Ellison founded Software Development Laboratories. In 1978, the couple divorced. Wheeler gave up any claim on her husband's company for $500.</li>
<li>Barbara Boothe from 1983 to 1986. Boothe was a former receptionist at Relational Software Inc. (RSI).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> They had two children, <a href="/wiki/David_Ellison" title="David Ellison">David</a> and <a href="/wiki/Megan_Ellison" title="Megan Ellison">Megan</a>, who are film producers at <a href="/wiki/Skydance_Media" title="Skydance Media">Skydance Media</a> and <a href="/wiki/Annapurna_Pictures" title="Annapurna Pictures">Annapurna Pictures</a>, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Melanie Craft, a <a href="/wiki/Romance_novel" title="Romance novel">romance novelist</a>, from 2003 to 2010. They married on December 18, 2003, at his Woodside estate. Ellison's friend <a href="/wiki/Steve_Jobs" title="Steve Jobs">Steve Jobs</a>, former CEO and co-founder of <a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc." title="Apple Inc.">Apple Inc.</a>, was the official wedding photographer,<sup id="cite_ref-San_Francisco_Chronicle_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-San_Francisco_Chronicle-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> and Representative <a href="/wiki/Tom_Lantos" title="Tom Lantos">Tom Lantos</a> officiated. They divorced in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>Ellison made a brief cameo appearance in the 2010 movie <i><a href="/wiki/Iron_Man_2" title="Iron Man 2">Iron Man 2</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-&#39;&#39;Forbes&#39;&#39;_Iron_Man2_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-&#39;&#39;Forbes&#39;&#39;_Iron_Man2-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> In 2010, Ellison purchased a 50% share of the <a href="/wiki/BNP_Paribas_Open" class="mw-redirect" title="BNP Paribas Open">BNP Paribas Open</a> tennis tournament.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> Ellison owns many exotic cars, including an <a href="/wiki/Audi_R8_(road_car)" class="mw-redirect" title="Audi R8 (road car)">Audi R8</a> and a <a href="/wiki/McLaren_F1" title="McLaren F1">McLaren F1</a>. His favorite is the <a href="/wiki/Acura_NSX" class="mw-redirect" title="Acura NSX">Acura NSX</a>, which he was known to give as gifts each year during its production.<sup id="cite_ref-Being_Larry_Ellison_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Being_Larry_Ellison-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Ellison is also reportedly the owner of a <a href="/wiki/Lexus_LFA" title="Lexus LFA">Lexus LFA</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Yachts">Yachts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Larry_Ellison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Yachts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2010, Ellison ended his ownership of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_motor_yachts_by_length" title="List of motor yachts by length">12th largest</a> <a href="/wiki/Yacht" title="Yacht">yacht</a> in the world, named <i><a href="/wiki/Rising_Sun_(yacht)" title="Rising Sun (yacht)">Rising Sun</a></i>. He sold his remaining shares in the yacht to music and film mogul <a href="/wiki/David_Geffen" title="David Geffen">David Geffen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> <i>Rising Sun</i> is 453 feet (138 metres) long,<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> and reportedly cost over $200<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million to build. He downsized to <i><a href="/wiki/Musashi_(yacht)" title="Musashi (yacht)">Musashi</a></i>, a 288-foot (88-metre) yacht built by <a href="/wiki/Feadship" title="Feadship">Feadship</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Yacht_racing">Yacht racing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Larry_Ellison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Yacht racing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Ellison competes in yachting through <a href="/wiki/Oracle_Team_USA" title="Oracle Team USA">Oracle Team USA</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> Following success racing <a href="/wiki/Maxi_yacht" title="Maxi yacht">Maxi yachts</a>, Ellison founded <a href="/wiki/BMW_Oracle_Racing" class="mw-redirect" title="BMW Oracle Racing">BMW Oracle Racing</a> to compete for the <a href="/wiki/2003_Louis_Vuitton_Cup" title="2003 Louis Vuitton Cup">2003 Louis Vuitton Cup</a>.
</p><p>In 2002, Ellison's Oracle's team introduced kite yachting into the America's Cup environment. Kite sail flying lasting about 30 minutes was achieved during testing in New Zealand.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>BMW Oracle Racing was the "Challenger of Record" on behalf of the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Gate_Yacht_Club" title="Golden Gate Yacht Club">Golden Gate Yacht Club</a> of San Francisco for the <a href="/wiki/2007_America%27s_Cup" title="2007 America&#39;s Cup">2007 America's Cup</a> in <a href="/wiki/Valencia_(city_in_Spain)" class="mw-redirect" title="Valencia (city in Spain)">Valencia, Spain</a>, until eliminated from the <a href="/wiki/2007_Louis_Vuitton_Cup" title="2007 Louis Vuitton Cup">2007 Louis Vuitton Cup</a> challenger-selection series in the semi-finals. On February 14, 2010, Ellison's yacht <i><a href="/wiki/USA_17_(yacht)" class="mw-redirect" title="USA 17 (yacht)">USA 17</a></i> won the second race (in the best of three "<a href="/wiki/Deed_of_Gift_of_the_America%27s_Cup" title="Deed of Gift of the America&#39;s Cup">deed of gift</a>" series) of the <a href="/wiki/2010_America%27s_Cup" title="2010 America&#39;s Cup">33rd America's Cup</a>, after winning the first race two days earlier. Securing a historic victory, Ellison and his BMW Oracle team became the first challengers to win a "deed of gift" match. The Cup returned to American shores for the first time since 1995. Ellison served as a crew member in the second race.<sup id="cite_ref-ESPN_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ESPN-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> Previously, Ellison had filed several legal challenges, through the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Gate_Yacht_Club" title="Golden Gate Yacht Club">Golden Gate Yacht Club</a>, against the way that <a href="/wiki/Ernesto_Bertarelli" title="Ernesto Bertarelli">Ernesto Bertarelli</a> (also one of the world's richest men) proposed to organize the <a href="/wiki/33rd_America%27s_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="33rd America&#39;s Cup">33rd America's Cup</a> following the 2007 victory of Bertarelli's team <a href="/wiki/Alinghi" title="Alinghi">Alinghi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ESPN_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ESPN-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> The races were finally held<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (July 2010)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> in February 2010 in Valencia.
</p><p>On September 25, 2013, Ellison's Oracle Team USA defeated <a href="/wiki/Emirates_Team_New_Zealand" class="mw-redirect" title="Emirates Team New Zealand">Emirates Team New Zealand</a> to win the <a href="/wiki/34th_America%27s_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="34th America&#39;s Cup">34th America's Cup</a> in <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Bay" title="San Francisco Bay">San Francisco Bay</a>, California.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> Oracle Team USA had been penalized two points in the final for cheating by some team members during the America's Cup World Series warm-up events.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> The Oracle team came from a 1–8 deficit to win 9–8, in what has been called "one of the greatest comebacks in sports history".<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Oracle Racing lost the <a href="/wiki/2017_America%27s_Cup" title="2017 America&#39;s Cup">2017 America's Cup</a> to Team New Zealand.
</p><p>In 2019, Ellison, in conjunction with <a href="/wiki/Russell_Coutts" title="Russell Coutts">Russell Coutts</a>, started the <a href="/wiki/SailGP" title="SailGP">SailGP</a> international racing series.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> The series used <a href="/wiki/F50_(catamaran)" title="F50 (catamaran)">F50</a> foiling catamarans, the fastest class of boat in history with regattas held across the globe. Ellison committed to five years of funding to support the series until it could become self sustaining. The first season was successful with global audiences of over 1.8 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Aviation">Aviation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Larry_Ellison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Aviation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Ellison is a licensed pilot who has owned several aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-Rohrlich_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rohrlich-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> He was cited by the city of <a href="/wiki/San_Jose,_California" title="San Jose, California">San Jose, California</a>, for violating its <a href="/wiki/Noise_mitigation#Aircraft_noise_abatement" class="mw-redirect" title="Noise mitigation">limits on late-night takeoffs and landings</a> from <a href="/wiki/San_Jose_Mineta_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="San Jose Mineta International Airport">San Jose Mineta International Airport</a> by planes weighing more than 75,000&#160;pounds (34,019&#160;kg). In January 2000, Ellison sued over the interpretation of the airport rule, contending that his <a href="/wiki/Gulfstream_V" title="Gulfstream V">Gulfstream V</a> aircraft "is certified by the manufacturer to fly at two weights: 75,000 pounds, and at 90,000 pounds for heavier loads or long flights requiring more fuel. But the pilot only lands the plane in San Jose when it weighs 75,000 pounds or less, and has the logs to prove it."<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> US District Judge <a href="/wiki/Jeremy_Fogel" title="Jeremy Fogel">Jeremy Fogel</a> ruled in Ellison's favor in June 2001, calling for a waiver for Ellison's jet, but did not invalidate the curfew.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Ellison also owns at least two military jets: a <a href="/wiki/SIAI-Marchetti_S.211" title="SIAI-Marchetti S.211">SIAI-Marchetti S.211</a>, a training aircraft designed in Italy, and a decommissioned <a href="/wiki/MiG-29" class="mw-redirect" title="MiG-29">MiG-29</a>, which the US government has refused him permission to import.<sup id="cite_ref-Rohrlich_10-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rohrlich-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tennis">Tennis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Larry_Ellison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Tennis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2009, Larry purchased the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Wells_Tennis_Garden" title="Indian Wells Tennis Garden">Indian Wells Tennis Garden</a> tennis facility in California's <a href="/wiki/Coachella_Valley" title="Coachella Valley">Coachella Valley</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Wells_Masters" title="Indian Wells Masters">Indian Wells Masters</a> tournament, both of which he still owns.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Homes">Homes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Larry_Ellison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Homes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Ellison styled his estimated $110&#160;million <a href="/wiki/Woodside,_California" title="Woodside, California">Woodside, California</a>, estate after <a href="/wiki/Feudal_Japan" class="mw-redirect" title="Feudal Japan">feudal Japanese</a> <a href="/wiki/Japanese_architecture" title="Japanese architecture">architecture</a>, complete with a man-made 2.3-acre (0.93&#160;ha) lake and an extensive <a href="/wiki/Seismic_retrofit" title="Seismic retrofit">seismic retrofit</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> In 2004 and 2005 he purchased more than 12 properties in <a href="/wiki/Malibu,_California" title="Malibu, California">Malibu, California</a>, worth more than $180&#160;million. The $65&#160;million Ellison spent on five contiguous lots at <a href="/wiki/Malibu,_California" title="Malibu, California">Malibu's</a> Carbon Beach made this the most costly residential transaction in United States history until <a href="/wiki/Ron_Perelman" class="mw-redirect" title="Ron Perelman">Ron Perelman</a> sold his <a href="/wiki/Palm_Beach,_Florida" title="Palm Beach, Florida">Palm Beach, Florida</a>, compound for $70&#160;million later that same year.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> His entertainment system cost $1&#160;million, and includes a rock concert-sized video projector at one end of a drained swimming pool, using the gaping hole as a giant subwoofer.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In early 2010, Ellison purchased the <a href="/wiki/Astor%27s_Beechwood_Mansion" class="mw-redirect" title="Astor&#39;s Beechwood Mansion">Astor's Beechwood Mansion</a>&#160;– formerly the summer home of the <a href="/wiki/Astor_family" title="Astor family">Astor family</a>&#160;– in <a href="/wiki/Newport,_Rhode_Island" title="Newport, Rhode Island">Newport, Rhode Island</a>, for $10.5&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>In 2011 he purchased the 249-acre Porcupine Creek Estate and private golf course in <a href="/wiki/Rancho_Mirage,_California" title="Rancho Mirage, California">Rancho Mirage, California</a>, for $42.9&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_74-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> The property was formerly the home of <a href="/wiki/Yellowstone_Club" title="Yellowstone Club">Yellowstone Club</a> founders <a href="/wiki/Edra_Blixseth" class="mw-redirect" title="Edra Blixseth">Edra</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tim_Blixseth" title="Tim Blixseth">Tim Blixseth</a>, and was sold to Ellison by creditors following their divorce and bankruptcy.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>On June 21, 2012, the governor of Hawaii, <a href="/wiki/Neil_Abercrombie" title="Neil Abercrombie">Neil Abercrombie</a>, declared that Ellison had signed an agreement to buy most of the island of <a href="/wiki/Lanai" title="Lanai">Lanai</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Castle_%26_Cooke" title="Castle &amp; Cooke">Castle &amp; Cooke</a> company, owned by <a href="/wiki/David_H._Murdock" title="David H. Murdock">David H. Murdock</a>. Following the purchase Ellison owns 98% of Lanai, Hawaii's sixth-largest island.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In December 2020, he left California and moved to Hawaii.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Philanthropy">Philanthropy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Larry_Ellison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Philanthropy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1992 Ellison shattered his elbow in a high-speed bicycle crash. After receiving treatment at <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Davis" title="University of California, Davis">University of California, Davis</a>, Ellison donated $5&#160;million to seed the Lawrence J. Ellison Musculo-Skeletal Research Center. In 1998, the Lawrence J. Ellison Ambulatory Care Center opened on the <a href="/wiki/Sacramento,_California" title="Sacramento, California">Sacramento</a> campus of the <a href="/wiki/UC_Davis_Medical_Center" title="UC Davis Medical Center">UC Davis Medical Center</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>To settle an <a href="/wiki/Insider_trading" title="Insider trading">insider trading</a> lawsuit arising from his selling nearly $1&#160;billion of Oracle stock, a court allowed Ellison to donate $100&#160;million to his own charitable foundation without admitting wrongdoing. A California judge refused to allow Oracle to pay Ellison's legal fees of $24&#160;million. Ellison's lawyer had argued that if Ellison were to pay the fees, that could be construed as an admission of guilt. His charitable donations to <a href="/wiki/Stanford_University" title="Stanford University">Stanford University</a> raised questions about the independence of two Stanford professors who evaluated the case's merits for Oracle.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> In response to the <a href="/wiki/September_11,_2001_attacks" class="mw-redirect" title="September 11, 2001 attacks">September 11 terrorist attacks</a> of 2001, Ellison made a controversial offer to donate software to the federal government<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> that would have enabled it to build and run a national identification database and to issue <a href="/wiki/Identity_documents_in_the_United_States" title="Identity documents in the United States">ID cards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i>Forbes</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span> 2004 list of charitable donations made by the wealthiest 400 Americans stated that Ellison had donated<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (January 2019)">when?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> $151,092,103, about 1% of his estimated personal wealth.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> In June 2006, Ellison announced he would not honor his earlier pledge of $115&#160;million to <a href="/wiki/Harvard_University" title="Harvard University">Harvard University</a>, claiming it was due to the departure of former President <a href="/wiki/Lawrence_Summers" title="Lawrence Summers">Lawrence Summers</a>. Oracle spokesman Bob Wynne announced, "It was really Larry Summers' brainchild and once it looked like Larry Summers was leaving, Larry Ellison reconsidered&#160;... [I]t was Larry Ellison and Larry Summers that had initially come up with this notion."<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> In 2007 Ellison pledged $500,000 to fortify a <a href="/wiki/Community_centre" title="Community centre">community centre</a> in <a href="/wiki/Sderot" title="Sderot">Sderot</a>, <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>, after discovering that the building was not fortified against rocket attacks.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> Other charitable donations by Ellison include a $10&#160;million donation to the <a href="/wiki/Friends_of_the_Israel_Defense_Forces" title="Friends of the Israel Defense Forces">Friends of the Israel Defense Forces</a> in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> In 2017 Ellison again donated to the Friends of the Israel Defense Forces, this time for $16.6&#160;million. His donation was intended to support the construction of well-being facilities on a new campus for <a href="/wiki/Co-ed" class="mw-redirect" title="Co-ed">co-ed</a> conscripts.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In August 2010 a report listed Ellison as one of the 40 billionaires who had signed "<a href="/wiki/The_Giving_Pledge" title="The Giving Pledge">The Giving Pledge</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In May 2016 Ellison donated $200&#160;million to the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Southern_California" title="University of Southern California">University of Southern California</a> for establishing a cancer research center: the Lawrence J. Ellison Institute for Transformative Medicine of USC.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_involvement">Political involvement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Larry_Ellison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Political involvement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Secretary_Pompeo_Meets_with_the_Oracle_Leadership_Team_(49391194042).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Secretary_Pompeo_Meets_with_the_Oracle_Leadership_Team_%2849391194042%29.jpg/220px-Secretary_Pompeo_Meets_with_the_Oracle_Leadership_Team_%2849391194042%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="176" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Secretary_Pompeo_Meets_with_the_Oracle_Leadership_Team_%2849391194042%29.jpg/330px-Secretary_Pompeo_Meets_with_the_Oracle_Leadership_Team_%2849391194042%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Secretary_Pompeo_Meets_with_the_Oracle_Leadership_Team_%2849391194042%29.jpg/440px-Secretary_Pompeo_Meets_with_the_Oracle_Leadership_Team_%2849391194042%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1639" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Secretary_Pompeo_Meets_with_the_Oracle_Leadership_Team_(49391194042).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ellison (right) with Secretary of State <a href="/wiki/Mike_Pompeo" title="Mike Pompeo">Mike Pompeo</a> in 2020</div></div></div>
<p>Ellison was critical of <a href="/wiki/National_Security_Agency" title="National Security Agency">NSA</a> whistle-blower <a href="/wiki/Edward_Snowden" title="Edward Snowden">Edward Snowden</a>, saying that "Snowden had yet to identify a single person who had been 'wrongly injured' by the NSA's data collection".<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> He has donated to both <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican</a> politicians,<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> and in late 2014 hosted Republican Senator <a href="/wiki/Rand_Paul" title="Rand Paul">Rand Paul</a> at a fundraiser at his home.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Ellison was one of the top donors to Conservative Solutions PAC, a super <a href="/wiki/Political_action_committee" title="Political action committee">PAC</a> supporting <a href="/wiki/Marco_Rubio" title="Marco Rubio">Marco Rubio</a>'s 2016 presidential bid. As of February 2016, Ellison had given $4&#160;million overall to the PAC.<sup id="cite_ref-RubioPAC_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RubioPAC-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> In 2020, Ellison allowed <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a> to have a fundraiser at his <a href="/wiki/Rancho_Mirage,_California" title="Rancho Mirage, California">Rancho Mirage</a> estate,<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> but Ellison was not present.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Recognition">Recognition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Larry_Ellison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Recognition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In 1997, Ellison received the Golden Plate Award of the <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Achievement" title="Academy of Achievement">American Academy of Achievement</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2013, Ellison was inducted into the Bay Area Business Hall of Fame.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2019, the Lawrence J. Ellison Institute for Transformative Medicine of USC honored Ellison with the first Rebels With A Cause Award in recognition of his generous support through the years.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Larry_Ellison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
